25:T4beb,<entryFree id="n13500" key="دُونً" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">دُونً</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">دون</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">دونن</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Low, base, vile, mean, paltry, inconsiderable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">contemptible;</hi> (Fr, T, S, M, * Msb, K;) applied to a man &amp;c.: (T, Msb:) and <hi rend="ital">inferior,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">lower, baser, viler,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">in grounds of pretension to respect</hi> or <hi rend="ital">honour</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">in any approvable quality</hi>]: (Lth, T:) and <hi rend="ital">such as falls short</hi> [of a thing]; used in this sense as a prefixed noun: (Ham p. 686:) [see below what is said of its usage as a prefixed noun by Lth and by Sb: and used as an epithet, <hi rend="ital">scanty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">deficient;</hi> applied to anything:] and <hi rend="ital">of a middling sort; between good and bad;</hi> applied to a man and to a commodity: (M:) and also <hi rend="ital">high,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">eminent, in rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition; noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">honourable:</hi> (T, K:) thus it bears two contr. significations (K) [and significations intermediate between those two]. A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا مَا عَلَا المَرْءُ رَامَ العَلَآء</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَيَقْتَعُ بِالدُّونِ مَنْ كَانَا دُونَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">When the man is high</hi> in rank, or nobility, <hi rend="ital">he seeks highness: and he who is low is content with that which is low</hi>]. (S.) Accord. to the most common usage, (Msb,) or accord. to what is asserted to be the most common usage, (Lh, M,) one says <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ مِنْ دُونٍ</foreign> (T, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">شَىْءٌ مِنْ دُونٍ</foreign> (M, Msb) <hi rend="ital">A man who is</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of a kind that is</hi>] <hi rend="ital">low, base,</hi> &amp;c., and <hi rend="ital">a thing that is</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of a kind that is</hi>] <hi rend="ital">low, base,</hi> &amp;c.: (Msb:) but sometimes they said <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ دُونٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَىْءٌ دُونٌ</foreign>, without <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>; (M, Msb;) and <foreign lang="ar">ثَوْبٌ دُونٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">a bad</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">an inferior</hi>] <hi rend="ital">garment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piece of cloth:</hi> (M:) or one should not say <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ دُونٌ</foreign>; (T, K;) for the Arabs did not use this phrase. (T.) <hi rend="ital">Accord.</hi> to Lth, one says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا دُونُ ذَاكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is the inferior of that</hi>], when meaning to denote by it low estimation, using the nom. case: (T:) [but this is uncommon, if allowable:] Sb says that <foreign lang="ar">دُون</foreign> is not used in the nom. case as a prefixed noun: as to the saying in the Kur [lxxii. 11, an instance similar to which occurs also in vii. 167], <foreign lang="ar">مِنَّا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الصَّالِحُونَ وَ مِنَّا دُونَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign>, the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">وَ مِنَّا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَوْمٌ دُونَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Of us are the righteous, and of us are a party below that party in rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">estimation</hi>]; (M, TA;) or, as another says, <foreign lang="ar">دون</foreign> is here in the accus. case but in the place of a noun in the nom. case because it is generally used as an adv. n. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  As an adv. n., <foreign lang="ar">دُون</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">Below,</hi> contr. of <foreign lang="ar">فَوْق</foreign>; (S, K;) <hi rend="ital">as denoting a falling short of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">right</hi> or <hi rend="ital">approved</hi>] <hi rend="ital">limit;</hi> (S;) or <hi rend="ital">denoting low,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mean, estimation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition;</hi> (Lth, T, M;) or <hi rend="ital">a condition lower, baser, viler,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">than that of another, in grounds of pretension to respect</hi> or <hi rend="ital">honour</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">in any approvable quality</hi>]; (Lth, T;) [and hence, <hi rend="ital">inferior to, beneath, under,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">short of,</hi> another <hi rend="ital">in rank, height, size,</hi> &amp;c.;] and <hi rend="ital">less than</hi> another, and <hi rend="ital">more deficient than</hi> another: (Fr, T:) and also <hi rend="ital">above; i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَوْق</foreign>; (T, K;) <hi rend="ital">in highness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">eminence, of rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in nobility;</hi> (T;) [and hence, <hi rend="ital">exceeding</hi> another, and <hi rend="ital">more than</hi> another:] thus bearing two contr. significations. (K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ دُونَكَ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">Zeyd is</hi> [<hi rend="ital">below thee,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">in a condition lower, baser, viler,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">than thine, in grounds of pretension to respect</hi> or <hi rend="ital">honour</hi> [&amp;c.]: and when one says, “ Verily such a one is high, or eminent, in rank or condition, ” or “ is noble, ” another replies, <foreign lang="ar">وَ دُونَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">And above that.</hi> (T.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Beneath, below in situation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">under;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">تَحْت</foreign>. (T, TA.) Using it in this sense, you say, <foreign lang="ar">دُوَن قَدَمِكَ خَدُّ عَدُوِّكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">May the cheek of thine enemy be beneath thy foot</hi>]: (T, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">جَلَسَ دُونَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He sat below him</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Before in respect of place,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in front:</hi> and [the contr., namely,] <hi rend="ital">behind,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beyond.</hi> (T, M, K.) [You may say, using it in the former sense, <foreign lang="ar">جَلَسَ دُونَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He sat before him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in front of him:</hi> (see Ham p. 86:) and, using it in the latter sense,] you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَمِيرٌ عَلَى مَا دُونَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَيْحُونَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This</hi> [man] <hi rend="ital">is governor,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">prince, over what is beyond</hi> [the river] <hi rend="ital">Jeyhoon.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَبْل</foreign> [generally signifying <hi rend="ital">Before in respect of time;</hi> but as some say, <hi rend="ital">in respect of place also,</hi> which may perhaps be here meant]: (T:) and [the contr., namely,] <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَعْد</foreign> [generally meaning <hi rend="ital">after in respect of time;</hi> but as <pb n="939"/> some say, <hi rend="ital">in respect of place</hi> also, which may perhaps be here meant]. (Fr, T, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  It signifies also <hi rend="ital">Nearer than</hi> another thing: (S, Msb, K:) so in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا دُونَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is nearer than that</hi>]; (S Msb;) or <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا دُونَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">this is nearer than he,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it</hi>]. (K.) [Hence,] one says also, <foreign lang="ar">اُدْنُ دُونَكَ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">Draw thou near in the space that is between me and thee:</hi> (A Heyth, T:) [or <hi rend="ital">approach thou nearer to me:</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">draw thou near</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">nearer</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to me.</hi> (IAar, T, M, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">يَزِيدُ بَغُضُّ الطَّرْفَ دُونِى</foreign>, a saying of a poet, means <hi rend="ital">Yezeed lowers the eye towards a spot between me and him.</hi> (A Heyth, T.) [<foreign lang="ar">خَشَعَتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دُونَهُ الأَبْصَارُ</foreign>, also, has a similar meaning: see 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">خشع</foreign>. So, too, has the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">خَاوَتَ طَرْفَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دُونِى</foreign>: see 3 in art. <foreign lang="ar">خوت</foreign>. And hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">دُونَ النَّهْرِ جَمَاعَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">In the way of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to, the river,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on this side of the river,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nearer than the river, is a company of men;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">before thy reaching the river</hi> [there is to be found, or encountered, <hi rend="ital">a company of men</hi>].                   <foreign lang="ar">الأَسَدِ أَهْوَالٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">In the way of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to, the slaying of the lion,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">before thine attaining to the slaying of the lion, terrors</hi> [are to be encountered]. (T, TA.) [And <foreign lang="ar">دُونَهُ خَرْطُ القَتَادِ</foreign>: see 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">خرط</foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">حَالَ دُونَ الشَّىْءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It intervened as an obstacle in the way to the thing;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">it prevented from attaining the thing.</hi> (W p. 71.) [And <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ دُونَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَىْءٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">There is nothing intervening as an obstacle in the way of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi>] And [hence,] <foreign lang="ar">قُتِلَ دُونَ مَالِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَخِيهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">جَارِهِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He was slain in defence of his property,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of himself,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of his brother,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of his neighbour.</hi> (Occurring in a trad. commencing with the words <foreign lang="ar">الغَرِيقُ شَهِيدٌ</foreign>, in the “ Jámi' es-Sagheer, ” and thus explained in the margin of a copy of that work.) [And <foreign lang="ar">نَبَحَ دُونَهُ</foreign> is a modern phrase meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He defended him as though by barking in the way to him.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  [Hence,] also <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">Against;</hi> denoting defence by means of intervention: see an ex. in a verse cited voce <foreign lang="ar">شَخْصٌ</foreign>]. (Fr, T, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">At, near, nigh, by,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">near by; with,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">present with;</hi> &amp;c.].                   </quote> (TA, but only the former hemistich is there given,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">And he made us to overtake the foremost</hi> of the wild animals, <hi rend="ital">while near to him were those that lagged behind, in a herd, not dispersed.</hi> (EM p. 48.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">غَيْر</foreign> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">Other than, beside,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">besides, exclusively of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">not</hi> as used before a substantive or an adjective]. (M, TA) with <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> prefixed to it, [very often in this case, in the Kur and elsewhere, as meaning <foreign lang="ar">غَيْر</foreign> and sometimes in other senses explained above,] and likewise with <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> (M, K, TA,) though rarely. (K.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا دُونَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا مِنْ دُونِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is below thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">above thee:</hi> &amp;c.]. (M, TA.) (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  It also denotes a command, (T, K,) and an incitement (Fr, T, S, K) to do a thing. (S.)                   <foreign lang="ar">دُونَكَ الدِّرْهَمَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Take thou the dirhem;</hi> (T;) or <foreign lang="ar">دُونَكَ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">دُونَكَ بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Take thou the thing:</hi> (M:) and using it in the latter sense, you say, <foreign lang="ar">دُونَكَهُ</foreign>, (S, K, TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">Keep thou, cleave thou, cling thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hold thou fast, to him;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">take care of him:</hi> (TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">دُنَكَ زَيْدًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Keep thou,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">to Zeyd, taking care of him.</hi> (T.) (S, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  And it also denotes a threat. (T, K.) (T, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  It is said that no verb is derived from it: (T, S, M, Msb:) but some assert that <foreign lang="ar">دَانَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أُدِينَ</foreign> [mentioned in the first paragraph of this art.] are derived from it.                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">دِيوَانٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ديوان</orth>
                  </form>, an arabicized word, (AO, M, Msb, &amp;c.,) from the Pers. [<foreign lang="ar">دِيوَانْ</foreign>]; (AO, M, &amp;c.;) [though some hold it to be of Arabic origin:] J says, (TA,) it is originally <foreign lang="ar">دِوَّانٌ</foreign>, but <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> is substituted for one of the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> s ; as is shown by its pl., (S, Msb,) which is <foreign lang="ar">دَوَاوِينُ</foreign>; (S, M, Msb, K;) for if the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> were radical, they would say <foreign lang="ar">دَيَاوِينُ</foreign>; (S;) but accord. to IDrd and IJ, (IB, TA,) it has this latter pl. also: (M, IB, K, TA:) Sb says that the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">دِيوَانٌ</foreign>, though after <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, is not changed into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, as it is in <foreign lang="ar">سَيِّدٌ</foreign>, because the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> in the former word is not inherent; that word being of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فِعَّالٌ</foreign>, from <foreign lang="ar">دَوَّنْتَ</foreign>; (M;) [i. e.] it is from <foreign lang="ar">دَوَّنَ الكُتُبَ</foreign> meaning “ he collected the writings; ” as is shown by their saying   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n13505-1" target="دُوَيْوِينٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n13507"/></foreign>, (M,) which is the dim.: (Msb:) ISk says that <foreign lang="ar">ديوان</foreign> is with kesr only [<hi rend="ital">to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">د</foreign>]; (M;) but one says   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n13505-2" target="دَيْوَانٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n13504"/></foreign> also, (K,) which is mentioned by Ks, as postclassical, and by Sb; like <foreign lang="ar">بَيْطَارٌ</foreign>: (M:) the meaning is <hi rend="ital">A</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَفْتَر</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">register</hi>]: (Shifá el-Ghaleel, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a collection of written leaves</hi> or <hi rend="ital">papers</hi> [<hi rend="ital">forming a book, generally for registration</hi>]: (ISk, M, Mgh, * K:) or <hi rend="ital">a register of accounts; an accountbook:</hi> (Msb:) and <hi rend="ital">a register of soldiers and pensioners</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and others</hi>]: (IAth, K:) the first who instituted, or appointed, or arranged, such a book, (Mgh, Msb, K,) among the Arabs, (Msb,) for the prefects, or administrators, (Mgh, Msb,) and the Kádees, (Mgh,) is said to have been 'Omar: (Mgh, Msb, K: *) accord. to El-Máwardee, it is <hi rend="ital">a register of what concerns the rights,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dues, of the state, relating to the acts of the government, and the finances, and the military and other administrators thereof:</hi> (TA:) then <hi rend="ital">any book</hi> was thus called: and especially the <hi rend="ital">poetry of some particular poet:</hi> so that this meaning became [conventionally regarded as] a proper signification thereof; (Shifá el-Ghaleel, TA;) i. e. <hi rend="ital">a collection of poetry</hi> [of a particular poet]. (TA.) [Hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ الدِّيوَانِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Such a one is of those whose names are written in the register.</hi> (Mgh.) [Also <hi rend="ital">Such a one is of the keepers of the register;</hi> or, <hi rend="ital">is of the registrars.</hi> (And sometimes it has another meaning, which see below.) And hence the saying] <foreign lang="ar">الشِّعْرُ دِيوَانُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العَرَبِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Poetry is the register of the Arabs</hi>]: because they used to refer to it on their differing in opinion respecting genealogies and wars or fights and the appointing of stipends or allowances from the government-treasury, like as the people of the <foreign lang="ar">ديوان</foreign> [properly so called] refer to their <foreign lang="ar">ديوان</foreign> in a case that is doubtful to them; or because it was the depository of their sciences, and the preserver of their rules of discipline, and the mine of their histories. (Har p. 263.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Afterwards, also, it was applied to signify <hi rend="ital">An account,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a reckoning.</hi> (Msb, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">Writers</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of accounts</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reckonings</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">A place of account</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reckoning,</hi> (Msb, TA,) and <hi rend="ital">of writers</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of accounts</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reckonings</hi>] (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [Also <hi rend="ital">A council, court,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tribunal:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">دَسْتٌ</foreign>. Hence <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُ الدِّيوَانِ</foreign> sometimes means <hi rend="ital">The people of the council, court,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tribunal.</hi>          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And also, in the present day, <hi rend="ital">A long seat, formed of a mattress laid against the side of a room, upon the floor or upon a raised structure</hi> or <hi rend="ital">frame, with cushions to lean against;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">two</hi> or <hi rend="ital">more of such mattresses &amp;c. similarly placed.</hi>] <pb n="940"/>
